I believe that the battery life on this clipper is very good. I was not able to drain the battery in my testing. Without an indication of battery charge, such testing would be inconvenient.<br /><br />No carrying case is provided. That's too bad, because it won't be easy to improvise one. A Ziploc bag, maybe. A real shame, because the clipper is small enough to travel with you. That's one of its advantages.<br /><br />The instruction manual advises that the clipper should be lubricated after each use. A tiny bottle of clipper oil is included for that purpose. This is inconvenient, but barber's clippers are supposed to be oiled up frequently as well. The oilable part of the Panasonic clipper snaps out easily. As long as Panasonic will sell replacements, the situation is not too bad. I don't plan to oil up my clipper frequently, so I expect the oilable part of the clipper to get dull or fall apart eventually. That's my choice, I'm lazy.<br /><br />I don't consider any of these complaints to be serious. I like this clipper. I found new jobs for it after I started using it. This reduces the opportunity for pinched hair for folks with particularly coarse facial hair, although I don't know many people with fine facial hair--so this might be a completely negligible consideration for most but the final point is that this trimmer will be less-likely to pinch hair and more apt to provide an even trim with fewer passes.<br /><br />I'm really in love with this, I appreciate the stand, that's purely aesthetically-pleasing though. The adjustability is quite fine tuned, in increments of .5mm (wow!).   842. REVIEW FOR SHAVER AS a \\"BODY GROOMING\\" DEVICE ONLY...<br /><br />The funny thing is that even the Panasonic website doesn't market this device as a \\"body groomer\\" but Amazon's website does. Regardless, I owned a Norelco goatee razor with a very similar design back in the mid-nineties. I utilized it for \\"dry\\" body hair trimming and it worked quite well. When I saw this had 19 different adjustments and could be used in the shower I was \\"all in\\". Upon receipt I observed that it is very lightweight, very modern, sleek and masculine looking. This is never a bad thing in regards to a -- \\"man groomer\\" tool. The long charging time (30 hours I believe) is a minor inconvenience. If I were still single and needed a quick groom before regular dates with hotties this would be a significant downside of this razor.<br /><br />ROUND 1:<br /><br />On my first trial in the shower I tried shaving \\"wet\\" WITHOUT any liquid body wash. That pointless experiment failed miserably. The \\"drag factor\\" with the razor on skin was unbelievably terrible...the guard on the razor just kept bouncing across the skin but cut very little. Thus, I immediately lathered up with body wash and began to shave away. I went with the lowest setting and that achieved a nearly \\"hairless look\\". Someone would have to be \\"up in your grill\\" to see that body hair was present on your body. Even with body wash applied I did have to hit some hairs from multiple angles. I didn't time it but I know I spent approximately 35-40 minutes in there to complete a FULL BODY SHAVE. Even still some hairs were missed due to having to \\"back track\\" and try and hit hairs from multiple angles. But overall it took care of 90% or so. And possibly this will improve as my skill with it improves.<br /><br />The razor didn't seem extremely powerful but maybe that is because it is very quiet and doesn't vibrate significantly. I used to trim with an Oster hair clipper and you get quite a vibration with the pro models (plugged into the wall). The clean-up with the Panasonic is easy as you simply hold it under a stream from your shower head. The hair frees itself from the comb area pretty easily and washes down the drain. This easy clean-up was the most compelling reason I was attracted to the idea of \\"wet shaving\\". When you \\"dry shave\\" with the Oster barber clippers hairs have a way of \\"flying away from you\\" and making a hand vacuum mandatory. Contrary to my Oster barber clippers I didn't have ingrown hairs running rampant post-shave with this Panasonic. Contrary to other Amazon reviewers opinions I thought the razor disassembled for cleaning quite easily. I did almost feel like I was going to break it given its lightweight materials and the way the guard pops off but it was no worse for the wear. The map pointing to where you are to oil the razor isn't perfectly diagrammed but you get the idea upon further examination.<br /><br />All in all, I think this is a very good product for BODY GROOMING with the only real recommendation being that a little more TORQUE to the motor may help cut those pesky hairs on the first go-around versus having to hit them from multiple angles. My body hairs aren't extremely coarse (like my facial hair) and it seems like I shouldn't have so many problematic hairs. However, since this same problem occurs with electric facial razors it is possibly just part of the reality of shaving and the way your hairs decide to grow in different directions.<br /><br />ROUND 2:<br /><br />The body groom on the lowest setting lasted about 2 weeks. I think this is pretty standard for body shaving. You go 3 weeks and it is just too hairy and doesn't look good. On this second attempt I used Dove Body Wash on a section of my body at a time (i.e. chest, left arm, right arm, left leg, right leg etc.) since soap dries quickly when you aren't under the water. This worked fairly well but I believe the ergonomics issue design of the shaver plus the human body (ex. difficultto shave lower leg due to bone or knee due to thin skin surrounding it etc.) it was not \\"easy as pie\\" to get the job done. On Round 2 I spent about 45 minutes in the shower and had to hit some areas twice and had to hit the hair from ALL DIFFERENT ANGLES to shave it off. By the end you really do just want it OVER as 45 minutes under the water makes you feel like a water mammal. Again, my hair isn't very coarse and I am a moderately hairy dude. NOTE: I did NOT shave the \\"goose neck\\" nor the \\"eggs\\". I don't believe this type of shaver is ideal for that but if you raise the guard high enough you're likely fine if you can pull the skin tawt. At the end of the day, I think 80-85% of the hair was \\"gonzo\\" but this left me doing a brief touch-up dry shave with this razor outside of the shower. I really do believe that it is either a WET SHAVE ELECTRIC issue OR a WEAK ASS MOTOR issue. This razor is the softest, quietest I've ever heard and it clearly does chop hair but if the manufacturer gave it MORE TORQUE I think I could finish shaving quicker and easier. I imagine someone with very coarse thick hair may have more issues than I've had given the not-so-powerful motor on this unit.<br /><br />My new rating for this shaver is: *** 1/2<br /><br />Depending on how long the lifespan is on this and future results I may consider a Norelco Body Groomer on my next go-around. We'll see...<br /><br />ROUND 3:<br /><br />I spent OVER 45 minutes in the shower doing \\"body grooming\\" (no goose neck or eggs) and even with MANY passes in all different directions I would say 25% of the hairs were missed. I used a \\"gel\\" type body soap and a Dove \\"creamy\\" type body wash. Neither worked much better than the other. As a result, I had to do dry shaving outside of the shower and even that didn't go smoothly (so-to-speak). I spent another 30 minutes cleaning up all the MISSED HAIRS and still ended up with 10 % of the hairs being missed. It's an amount which will likely only by noticed by your female friend but given how much time I spent I expected better results.<br /><br />The KEY PROBLEMS with this shaver APPEAR to be as follows:<br /><br />a) The MOTOR is a weak pile<br />b) The BLADE isn't sharp and thus barely cuts hairs and misses many so you have to hit them 12 times in all different directions<br /><br />As a result, my FINAL RATING = ** 1/2 stars.

  996. UPDATE: after using this trimmer for several months now, I've really grown attached to it. Changing review from 4 stars to 5.<br /><br />I love this trimmer and use it much more often than I do my other shaver that gives you a smooth shave (I use both, depending on the look I want for the day). Besides just the different overall look, I like using the trimmer over the shaver because 1) it's faster and 2) if you miss a spot, nobody is going to notice.<br /><br />The trimmer is waterproof-you can use it in the shower. The benefit to this is that this style of trimmer doesn't catch any hair--it just cuts it and lets it fall. Combine this with the fact that one who typically uses a trimmer instead of a close-shaver will have longer hair to trim, and you can wind up with a bit of a mess on the sink and down all over yourself. Personally, I prefer to just shave over the trash can and then shower after, but, hey, it's an option. The better application for the waterproof attribute is that you can just rinse the whole thing off after you use it which is nice because hair sticks to it, esp. if you recently oiled it. Oh, yes--having to oil it... that would be a con except that I think it's pretty normal for this style of cutter to need that. The fact that it is so easy to do and easy to clean makes it only a mild annoyance and since I'm not aware of clippers of this style that don't need oil, I'm not going to take any stars away. UPDATE: I've gotten really lazy and seldom oil it. It is still running just fine. When I can hear it run a little slower than usual, I oil it and it goes back to what it was. I don't recommend you get lazy too, but if you do, it's not the end of the world.<br /><br />The body is small and lightweight and easy to hold. The length adjuster (how close of a shave you want) is very precise from 1 mm up to 10mm, although I actually take the adjuster off and trim it to... I'm guessing... 1/2mm or so. It's very easy to make the adjustments and/or to remove the guard altogether.<br /><br />I have to admit, I'm not crazy about the recharging stand. I think they had to take this approach to make it safe for use in the shower, but I much prefer the normal charging method of plugging something into the body of the shaver itself. The stand is kinda' big and clunky and not as good when you are trying to keep the bathroom counter cleared off and looking neat and clean. UPDATE: I'm over it :)<br /><br />I also would have liked the motor to be just a bit stronger and/or faster to help prevent hair from being pulled instead of cut. I have this problem MUCH less with this trimmer than I do with the trimmer built into my shaver, but it still happens from time to time. UPDATE: I have noticed that as long as you cut with the blades parallel to your skin (as opposed to perpendicular), my hair is almost never pulled.<br /><br />So in summary<br /><br />Pros:<br />Quick and easy to shave<br />Quick and easy to clean and adjust<br />Small, light and easy to hold<br />Water proof<br /><br />Cons:<br />Charging base is a bit awkward<br />Motor could be beefed up just a bit<br />Just like all other clippers of this variety that I am aware of, it requires you to oil it.<br /><br />Recommended.

  999. [[VIDEOID:mo3OBC1WMIKYTZ7]]The ergonomics of the Panasonic Milano Men's All-in-one Hair and Beard Trimmer are not the best. The trimmer is light which is good for convenience but to the point of being so lightweight that it felt cheap and plastic. The trimmer is not well balanced and this coupled with the lightweight feel led to the feeling that it is more of a toy than a serious trimmer. The power button is located on the bottom which means that it is awkward to turn on the trimmer from the same position as you would hold it while using it.<br /><br />The trimmer blades must be oiled after each use and a small container of oil is included. A drop of oil must be applied in three spots. A diagram is included on the trimmer body so that you know where to apply the oil even if you misplace the owner's manual.<br /><br />The trimmer has an integrated comb rather than removable combs. The height of the integrated comb can be adjusted between 1mm and 10mm. If you want hair at a length longer than 10mm you are out of luck with this trimmer.<br /><br />As far as the trimming is concerned, the Panasonic trimmer works well and I had no problem using it. The combs do have a little give, but not a significant amount and the combs remain in place even if you apply a bit of force while pressing the trimmers against your face. Panasonic has done the comb design much better than some other brands. I only wish that you could extend the height beyond 10mm.<br /><br />A summary of some of the pros and cons of the Panasonic Milano Men's All-in-one Hair and Beard Trimmer as discussed in the video are:<br /><br />Pros:<br />- Can be used in the shower or under other wet conditions<br />- Rather than to use combs to adjust the height of the trim, the trimmer has an integrated comb, the height of which is controlled with a dial on the side of the clippers<br />- The comb can easily be removed to allow for the blades to be cleaned or to allow for fine trimming, for example squaringside burns.<br />- Lightweight, but bordering on feeling too light<br />- Quieter than other trimmers that I have used<br />- Comb height does not change even when you press the trimmer against your face<br /><br />Cons<br />- The maximum height of the comb is 10mm. If you like your facial hair to be longer than that the clippers will not work for you.<br />- The blades must be oiled before each use<br />- The on / off button is inconveniently located<br />- Long charge times<br /><br />Overall, I would recommend the Panasonic Milano Men's All-in-one Hair and Beard Trimmer only to people who want to take advantage of the ability to use the trimmer in a wet environment. Otherwise, I would recommend a clipper like the Remington Titanium Precision Pro instead because it offers greater flexibility for different lengths of hair. The Remington comes with a collection of combs which allows for a much greater range of cutting heights, has better ergonomics and does not require oiling after each use.

However, you could probably get away with less frequent oiling without causing any problems. Personally, I've been oiling it after every 3 or 4 uses.   1160. This is a really good rechargeable beard trimmer intended for regularly maintained beard or facial hair. The cutting dial allows for highly precise length adjustments, from 1mm to 10mm, in half millimeter intervals along the way. So if you're really particular about the exact length of your beard, then this one should give all the control anyone needs.<br /><br />The charging base is nice - just place the shaver into it and a red LED lights up letting you know it's charging (FYI - the red LED does Not go out once fully charged, it just stays illuminated the whole time the shaver is in the base.) The base is a perfect cradle for this shaver; it doesn't needlessly cling to the shaver, so it can easily be removed and placed back with one hand. The metallic blue shaft and silver accent gives the shaver a chic look. And most importantly, it does cut quite well and is relatively silent. I did notice the blades don't have quite the same, rock steady cutting power of a plugged in shaver, but that's to be expected with most rechargeable battery shavers. But for regular use, it's a fair trade off to not have a cord dangling in my way. This will probably be my go-to shaver for regular maintenance. But if I ever decide to mow down to a goatee, or let my beard get a bit too long between touch-ups, then I'd probably reach for the full cutting power of my plug-in Wahl, since it can mow through anything with relative ease.<br /><br />I'm not sure the wet/dry feature of this shaver is very meaningful; those are best for a clean shave and easy cleanup. But for facial hair maintenance, the wet/dry thing is pretty much a meaningless gimmick; you'll pluck as many hairs as you trim if trying to touch-up a wet beard, and rinsing longer stubble off the blades wont be as effective as just brushing them off. (Yes, a small brush is included.)<br /><br />Bottom Line - this is a really good beard trimmer that feels nice in the hand, and offers excellent precision and cutting ability for regularly maintained beards.for regularly maintained beards.

  1179. I've only used it a couple of times, but it is so far the best facial trimmer I've ever used. I've used Norelco in the past, and they were pretty decent, but I had to make several passes over my beard to get all the hair even. With the Panasonic Milano ER-GB40-S, it takes two passes at the most. You just have to make sure you go against the grain, especially my beard hairs go in all different directions. From what I can see, there are two things this beard trimmer has over the competition. First, the adjustable comb that has 19 length settings. Sure, other facial trimmers have adjustable combs, but they're often flimsy and interfere with the hair making contact with the blades. Second, there's a small groove in the comb in which the hair is not obstructed by the blade. This simple addition is mind-blowingly effective in making sure that the comb keeps the hair at the selected level without interfering with it's contact with the blades. The only CON is that you have to take apart the blade assembly to clean and oil it. And, according to the manual/instructions, you're supposed to do this after you use it each time. Despite that, I'm a life-long Panasonic facial trimmer user now. I can confidently state that I will always own this trimmer or the closest version Panasonic has to offer well into the future, because my beard has never looked this good before with so little effort.
